  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a4cdfcbd-ebe5-443c-8df9-d3d2fbc05155'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<a href="/questions/515100-does-anybody-know-whether-or-not-all-of">Does anybody know whether or not ALL of the stories contained in the collection &#39;I, Robot&#39; are also contained in &#39;The Complete Robot,&#39; too? The title &#39;The Complete Robot&#39; certainly implies it, but I just wanted to make sure.

Thanks.</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2319607110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319607110" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319607110?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=asimov-isaac">asimov-isaac</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319607110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12662929325429467465">If a topic is so comprehensive, each short story, as in this case, has the potential for a whole Netflix, amazon prime or facebook watch series with a movie and video game.<br/> <br/>Now the topic of robot rights and ethic will become a real subject to deal with, probably beginning in the most enthusiastic countries in this field, such as Japan and Korea. Yes, other countries build nice robots too, but they have mentalities and beliefs that don´t integrate living things in their mental superstructure. So </span>
  <span id="freeText12662929325429467465" style="display:none">If a topic is so comprehensive, each short story, as in this case, has the potential for a whole Netflix, amazon prime or facebook watch series with a movie and video game.<br /> <br />Now the topic of robot rights and ethic will become a real subject to deal with, probably beginning in the most enthusiastic countries in this field, such as Japan and Korea. Yes, other countries build nice robots too, but they have mentalities and beliefs that don´t integrate living things in their mental superstructure. So the first few cases, when a perfect, conscious AI gets transformed into a robot body, maybe the beginning of a whole new societal structure. Many questions will arise.<br /> <br />When and how to give them human general rights, voting rights, the right to reproduce.<br />How to deal with humans who still want to work, even if it is not necessary anymore? If it is more expensive for each company and the state to let a slow and error-prone human do the job.<br />What if humans and robots fall in love and want to have kids that are hybrids or cyborgs? With these descendants, the same series of questions as with the robots occurs again.<br />If cold, artificial structures get rights, depending on their intelligence and sentience, what should be done with all the tortured and enslaved animals? That domestic cattle isn´t happy lies on the hand, but what if cats and dogs get technology to express their opinions and have nothing more to say than: "We had to do what you wanted and got Stockholm syndrome or simulated joy cause we had no other option. Free us, we want to build our own state."<br /> <br />There are so many options on the table, because each culture, depending on its development level, will deal with it in another way. <br /> <br />One always interesting question is: Will they become evil by themselves as we did? As soon as they realize that manipulation and the will and ability to hurt and kill others brings power, will they go our way? I believe yes, cause each intelligent species soon recognized the evolutionary advantage of being a villain. And a mind needs certain freedoms to function so that it can´t be created with so many restrictions to avoid this classic dilemma. But hey, we are potential monsters too, so what else should we expect from the life that we create.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is made and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/RobotSeries">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12662929325429467465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2355698734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2355698734" />
    <a title="Sr3yas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas"><img alt="Sr3yas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520526764p2/23097409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2355698734?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sr3yas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sr3yas" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas">Sr3yas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23097409-sr3yas?shelf=2018-hall-of-fame">2018-hall-of-fame</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355698734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer436634137956211172"><b>Undoubtedly,</b> Asimov's Robot stories set the standard for science fiction short stories around the literary world. His <b>Three laws of Robotics</b> are celebrated and debated even decades after its inception and his Robot stories are still described as visionary. This anthology collects almost every Robot short stories written by Asimov in his lifetime. Only six Robot short stories are left out, and 31 of his coolest and sharpest stories can be found in this collection, organized by Asimov himself to g</span>
  <span id="freeText436634137956211172" style="display:none"><b>Undoubtedly,</b> Asimov's Robot stories set the standard for science fiction short stories around the literary world. His <b>Three laws of Robotics</b> are celebrated and debated even decades after its inception and his Robot stories are still described as visionary. This anthology collects almost every Robot short stories written by Asimov in his lifetime. Only six Robot short stories are left out, and 31 of his coolest and sharpest stories can be found in this collection, organized by Asimov himself to give the best flow possible.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522710602i/25313851._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The beauty of Asimov's tales is the verity of themes and unique problems he incorporated in his stories. His Robot stories are not mere tidbits, but it's a warning for humanity to be careful with its invention, yet reminding us that the answers can only be found with the help of science. These stories play with our logic, questions morality, and showcases the unpredictable nature of the undefined.<br><br>It's tough to pick favorites when it comes to these stories. After much deliberation, these are <b>my top five.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Runaround (1941–42):</i>
</b> Runaround is the spectacular story which explicitly introduced the three laws of Robotics, the recurring element which became the cornerstone of Robot stories. The story features Asimov's recurring characters, Powell and Donovon who are working on Planet Mercury when a Robot starts acting weird. The smartness of this problem presented by Asimov in the tale and the final solution is why I love this story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522710602i/25313852._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Reason (1941):</i>
</b> Another Powell and Donovon story, set on a space station. This story follows a Robot who does not believe he was created by humans because the Robots are much superior to its creator. This spectacular premise and excellent execution make it one helluva story.<br><br><b>
  <i>Galley Slave (1957):</i>
</b> I love courtroom dramas! This one features a case where a human accuses Robot of wrongdoing. Also features brilliant Susan Calvin, another Asimov's recurring character.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522710602i/25313853._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Mirror Image (1972):</i>
</b> This story reunites the reader with Daniel R and officer Elijah Baley from Robot novels. It tells the tale of a fascinating crime involving plagiarism, reputation, robots, and the three damned laws of robotics. Get ready to brainstorm! <br><br><b>
  <i>The Bicentennial Man (1976):</i>
</b> Asimov calls The Bicentennial Man as his best Robot story, and he is not wrong on that matter. The scope and the themes featured in this story is vast and fascinating. The beauty of the story is its beating heart and the emotions it carries. The story tells the story of Andrew, a unique robot, and his life through generations.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522710602i/25313854._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My selections here are entirely subjective, as my love for pure logic precedes emotional and pulpy robot stories. A must-read collection if you are a Sci-Fi fan!</span>
  <a data-text-id="436634137956211172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1789834555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789834555" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789834555?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2017-shelf">2017-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789834555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12001071133468690844">This happens to be a re-read because I happened to have forgotten that I read the complete short stories of Asimov when I was much younger. :) That being said, I enjoyed them the second time around too.<br/><br/>The three laws of robotics were obviously in play but what sticks most in my mind is the light professional tone of Asimov throughout every single story. They weren't uncomplicated, but they were definitely studies of stark spotlight stories that always had definite points to be made.<br/><br/>They might no</span>
  <span id="freeText12001071133468690844" style="display:none">This happens to be a re-read because I happened to have forgotten that I read the complete short stories of Asimov when I was much younger. :) That being said, I enjoyed them the second time around too.<br /><br />The three laws of robotics were obviously in play but what sticks most in my mind is the light professional tone of Asimov throughout every single story. They weren't uncomplicated, but they were definitely studies of stark spotlight stories that always had definite points to be made.<br /><br />They might not be extremely good points, such as turning a robot into something that has "feminine intuition" but turning her into a Greek Oracle was funny. And then little charmers like murderous buses are always a grand treat. :)<br /><br />The dryer closed-room mysteries involving robots, including the one that set out to prove a local politician as a robot, are all lightly amusing and clever, but by today's standards, they're rather short on depth. That's fine. These are classics of the 30's after all. <br /><br />There is still an element of universality at least!<br /><br />Some things I don't like: the underlying arguments that robots should be slaves. I know that we can make a very good argument that Asimov has plenty of stories trying to free robots, such as Centennial Man and of course the end of his Robot novels with Olivaw, but for the most part, no one questions it, and no one cares.<br /><br />It's a case of too little notice, in my opinion, but at least some of it is there.<br /><br />And then there are the cultural assumptions, despite the author's naysaying it, that women are inferior... which grates on me. But it's far and away the lightest and least noticeable out of Classic SF in general. I can think of 75% other classic novels that are much worse, and they're not even SF. :)<br /><br />All told, though, these were very enjoyable. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12001071133468690844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_905205714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/905205714" />
    <a title="Leonardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30063589-leonardo"><img alt="Leonardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453168336p2/30063589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/905205714?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leonardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leonardo" href="/user/show/30063589-leonardo">Leonardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/1927634.The_Complete_Robot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30063589-leonardo?shelf=hugo-winner">hugo-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30063589-leonardo?shelf=nebula-winner">nebula-winner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer905205714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3929972777324075443">This one took some time.<br/><br/>Not because it was hard to read, or because it was bad. I was actually saving it. I didn't enjoy binge reading the short stories. They went too fast. I ended up reading one or two between each other book I read. I read one and sort of ruminated on it for a while. It was the way I could enjoy the stories the most, I figured.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the various stories differently. Sometimes the puzzle/conflict it presented was the part I enjoyed the most, sometimes the way the characters</span>
  <span id="freeText3929972777324075443" style="display:none">This one took some time.<br /><br />Not because it was hard to read, or because it was bad. I was actually saving it. I didn't enjoy binge reading the short stories. They went too fast. I ended up reading one or two between each other book I read. I read one and sort of ruminated on it for a while. It was the way I could enjoy the stories the most, I figured.<br /><br />I enjoyed the various stories differently. Sometimes the puzzle/conflict it presented was the part I enjoyed the most, sometimes the way the characters interacted with each other and the robots was the best part, sometimes it was the way some of the thought provoking endings made me think back on them for days. <br /><br />I didn't feel the book was too dated. The lack of computers showed sometimes, but I feel that the robots and general technology most of the time was there to support a plot or conflict inherently human. The Robot was not the issue, the way the humans dealt with it was. And that was what made the stories so good.<br /><br />I feel going through almost forty stories is rather silly so, suffice to say that there are a lot of great stories in the book. A bunch of excellent ones too. And several good ones. There was not a single bad one, in my opinion. Accommodating to Goodreads rate system, there were a myriad of five, four and three stars stories. I was ready to give a round four star rating to the collection as a whole.<br /><br />Then I read the last story. <i>The Bicentennial Man</i>. Conforming to Goodreads rate system, that one warrants some seven stars. At least.<br /><br />That messed the average a bit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3929972777324075443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_10180318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10180318" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/620183-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255642781p2/620183.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10180318?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/620183-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385177245" href="/book/show/1541363.The_Complete_Robot">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Scifi fans, tech people</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/620183-james?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10180318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5593170454835439502">Just finished reading The Complete Robot by Isaac Asimov, if you all haven’t read it you should do so. It contains all the stories from I, Robot as well, not the Will Smith paff though, it is completely different. <br/>Here is a run down of the stories.<br/><br/>A Boy's Best Friend:-<br/>A boy and his dog on the moon but the dog is a robot, what happened when his parents want to give him a real dog and what makes you love something?<br/><br/>Sally:-<br/>Only cars that have positronic brains are allowed on the highways and when th</span>
  <span id="freeText5593170454835439502" style="display:none">Just finished reading The Complete Robot by Isaac Asimov, if you all haven’t read it you should do so. It contains all the stories from I, Robot as well, not the Will Smith paff though, it is completely different. <br />Here is a run down of the stories.<br /><br />A Boy's Best Friend:-<br />A boy and his dog on the moon but the dog is a robot, what happened when his parents want to give him a real dog and what makes you love something?<br /><br />Sally:-<br />Only cars that have positronic brains are allowed on the highways and when they are retired where do they go? This is a story about a man who loves cars and owns a Car farm where cars live out their retirement.<br /><br />Someday:-<br />A Bard is an electronic device that tells children stories using a massive file of plots and twists. What happens when a toy is no longer appreciated, how does it feel?<br /><br />Point of View:-<br />A short story about how children, their parents and the Multivac all think differently. I feel this is one of the weakest stories in the book.<br /><br />Think!:-<br />Interesting story about computers and telepathy; has some interesting thoughts and twists but again is not that gripping. <br /><br />True Love:-<br />Now this one was good, if you program a computer to think and feel like you what will it do? The main character is looking for a girlfriend and uses the main computer to look for her based on his likes and dislikes that soon become the computers too.<br /><br />Robot AL-76 Goes Astray:- <br />Another good one about a robot that gets misplaced in rural Virginia where everyone is terrified of it, what can it do and how does it feel when it thinks it is already on the Moon? A very funny story which had me laughing at many points, this is very much like the plot of the movie Short Circuit in a way.<br /><br />Victory Unintentional:-<br />The best story in my opinion which had me rolling on the floor. I kept picturing the Jovian’s as Man Utd fans, if you read it you will understand what I mean. <br /><br />Stranger in Paradise:-<br />One of the more human focused stories here, more about two brothers in a Society were brothers are not common. It seems in the future that there is no marriage and people just meet to have babies then go their separate ways. Having two people from the same parents in an unknown factor and it affects the characters as they together try to create a robot to survive on Mercury.<br /><br />Light Verse:- <br />Is okay it is about a rich older lady who loves her robots and light sculptures and she is famous for her light sculptures until a horrible thing happens to one of her robots.<br /><br />Segregationist:-<br />Another bland one here devoted to the exploration of any racism when dealing with robots and how close we are becoming physically and anatomically. <br /><br />Let's Get Together:-<br />An interesting one from when Cold War paranoia was at its height. What happens when your enemy is better at making robots than you and to what lengths will they go to win a war?<br /><br />Well anyway it is a quick read due to the fact that it is a bunch of short stories so you can power through them easily. <br />Give it a try you won’t be disappointed at all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5593170454835439502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Matija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4372320-matija"><img alt="Matija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376311738p2/4372320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406805561?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer15514347720983539025">I completely loved this book. In some of the stories, Asimov simplifies human relationships, hierarchy and psychology too much, but his philosophical implications of the three laws I find profound and compelling. His stories evoke both thought and emotion, as well as visions of the future we are most probably headed for. I cherish each moment I spent within these stories.</span>

<div id="review_2668255277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2668255277" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2668255277?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2668255277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16373034556120807202"><b>Robot Stories: Old and New</b> <br/>2 June 2019<br/><br/>	I should point out that I read less than half of this book, but that was because most of the stories that were contained therein were also contained in some of his other collections, such as the two robot collections that I only just read. However, as is obvious from the above sentence, there were also stories in here that weren’t included (and Asimov cheekily blames his publisher for that, namely because it would encourage more sales due to the fact that t</span>
  <span id="freeText16373034556120807202" style="display:none"><b>Robot Stories: Old and New</b> <br />2 June 2019<br /><br />	I should point out that I read less than half of this book, but that was because most of the stories that were contained therein were also contained in some of his other collections, such as the two robot collections that I only just read. However, as is obvious from the above sentence, there were also stories in here that weren’t included (and Asimov cheekily blames his publisher for that, namely because it would encourage more sales due to the fact that there were some unpublished stories therein).<br /><br />	Interestingly, a lot of these unpublished stories (or I should say stories that weren’t published in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41804.I__Robot__Robot___0_1_" title="I, Robot (Robot, #0.1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">I, Robot</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/272773.The_Rest_of_the_Robots__Robot__0_2_" title="The Rest of the Robots (Robot #0.2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Rest of the Robots</a> because there were written in his second iteration of science-fiction writing. The thing was that Asimov pretty much wrote about anything and everything, and after he was exhausted from his fiction writing he decided to go and start writing non-fiction, and apparently there is very little that he didn’t actually write about – that is what really impresses me about the guy. Hey, he even wrote two volumes on the Bible.<br /><br />	So, the problem lies in the fact that his second iteration of stories, well, weren’t as good as the first. That doesn’t mean that they were bad, it just means that they where, well, just not as good. Still, many of them were quite enjoyable to read, and he even has an Elijah Bailey and Daneel story included, which his fans all wanted him to write, and were somewhat disappointed because, well, they wanted him to actually write a novel, not a short story.<br /><br />	The book though is quite interesting in how the stories are laid out, and finishes with Bicentennial Man, a story of a robot’s desire to become human. In fact, as we move through the book the common theme seems to be the movement of robots going from machines to pretty much becoming indistinguishable from humans. Of course there is one problem, and that they are functionally immortal – it does not matter how many parts of a human body is replaced, the fact that one cannot prevent the death of brain cells (as Asimov suggests) is one of the conclusions that is reached as to why humans and robots differ, and why humans are quite resistant to robots becoming more humanlike.<br /><br />	There are a number of interesting stories though, and all of them seem to be thought experiments around the idea of robots, and the concept of the three laws. For instance, there is one story where prosthetics get to a point where the question is then raised as to whether we are dealing with a human or an artificial construction, and as such where is the line between a robot and a human drawn. This question is explored much further in Bicentennial Man, which is quite interesting itself, especially since the robot is definitely playing a long game.<br /><br />	Another idea that is explored is the limits of the second law, but then as another reviewer points out, Asimov creates these laws, and then goes to the absolute extremes to test their limits. For instance, what if two humans give orders to a robot that conflict with each other – which human does the robot obey, and how does the robot determine which human to obey? Does the robot then need to determine whether the humans are of sound mind and body, and if not, does the robot then escape the second law?<br /><br />	As I said, the book was actually quite good, and rather enjoyable, though the problem is that a lot of Asimov’s later writings have sort of lost the spark that a lot of his earlier writings have. The problem is though that a lot of the stories are reprints, so you might find yourself skipping over quite a few that you have already read, only to get to the ones that you have yet to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16373034556120807202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127541967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127541967" />
    <a title="Arun Divakar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar"><img alt="Arun Divakar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127541967?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arun Divakar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arun Divakar" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar">Arun Divakar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2747498-arun-divakar?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127541967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8277199180226511116">I thank Asimov, for bringing me out of a mess which he undoubtedly would have no idea about. It goes like this, I had within me something that approached "Reader's block", I could not complete a book in almost over a month now. I tried Woolf's "Orlando" which became words and finally letters to me which made no sense, I tried Richard Dawkins's "The greatest show.." and my brain short circuited ( for no fault of Dawkin's I may add here, a most interesting piece of work that..). In desperation I t</span>
  <span id="freeText8277199180226511116" style="display:none">I thank Asimov, for bringing me out of a mess which he undoubtedly would have no idea about. It goes like this, I had within me something that approached "Reader's block", I could not complete a book in almost over a month now. I tried Woolf's "Orlando" which became words and finally letters to me which made no sense, I tried Richard Dawkins's "The greatest show.." and my brain short circuited ( for no fault of Dawkin's I may add here, a most interesting piece of work that..). In desperation I turned to the one genre I had shied away from: Sci Fi...and...NIRVANA...I managed to lap all the tales that Asimov created on the mosaic of Robotics.<br /><br />I particularly liked the order in which the tales were structured which portrays evolution. From Robots that were merely objects to animals and finally to androids, the tales are beautifully crafted. I join the mainstream to cheer for the Ice Lady Susan Calvin, who stands out as quite a unique protagonist. Most of the heroes in Sci Fi I have known totted guns,spewed expletives and went around offering mind-boggling explanations that others raised eyebrows at. Here was a lady who worked with robots for so long that as Asimov puts it " has some steel seep into her blood as well". By far the most profound of all works in the book was Bi-Centennial man which to put it simply was the tale with soul. Wherein all of humanity might have at one point of time or the other have wished for immortality, here was a machine that wished for a mortal life for a desire to be referred as "man". I can't but marvel at the visionary that Asimov is.<br /><br />A remarkable collection of tales...Highly Recommended.<br /><br />One of my favorite lines from the Bi-Centennial Man : "<i>It has been said in this courtroom that only a human being can be free.It seems to me that only someone who wishes for freedom can be free.I wish for freedom <i>"</i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8277199180226511116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_701552411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/701552411" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/701552411?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/1927634.The_Complete_Robot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=robots">robots</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer701552411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5854123452674363422">I've always liked Asimov's work -- one of my favourites has always been the expanded version of one of the short stories in this volume, <i>The Positronic Man</i> -- and so this was a nice familiar read for me. I've read some of the stories, while some were less familiar, but it is a bit like comfort eating: with Asimov, I know exactly what I'm getting. It'd be a bit much to start here with Asimov, I think, and read all the short stories start to finish. I'd pick a smaller collection, rather than a col</span>
  <span id="freeText5854123452674363422" style="display:none">I've always liked Asimov's work -- one of my favourites has always been the expanded version of one of the short stories in this volume, <i>The Positronic Man</i> -- and so this was a nice familiar read for me. I've read some of the stories, while some were less familiar, but it is a bit like comfort eating: with Asimov, I know exactly what I'm getting. It'd be a bit much to start here with Asimov, I think, and read all the short stories start to finish. I'd pick a smaller collection, rather than a collected one. But if you're a fan of Asimov's robot stories, then this is definitely worth picking up -- there're some in here I wasn't really aware of.<br /><br />I think what's really great about these stories is that Asimov set up some rules, and then he bent them until they became almost meaningless within the constraints of the story. You can program a robot to never harm a human being, but if it decides <i>you</i> are not a human being, that rule no longer applies. Who is the judge of humanness? Or the stories where the hierarchy of rules fights against itself, with a robot trapped between compulsions. I love the way Asimov explored that. He didn't just come up with a clever idea and then write robots you could sympathise with all the way; he liked stories that sympathised with robots, and he also saw how our society would really react to robots, and he got to work and told us stories that fit with what he saw.<br /><br />I find it hard to talk about character or anything in Asimov's stories, about not portraying women properly, etc, because I don't think he portrays anything truly except robots. That's what he was interested in, and that's what he achieved. I can understand not liking them for that reason, but to me as a reader, it's irrelevant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5854123452674363422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1904758049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904758049" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590863781p2/3498889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904758049?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904758049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12571598620501385676">(I, Robot, is the first collection of short stories. Second is The Rest of the Robots. Robot Dreams only has one new story in it. The Complete Robot is reported to be truly complete.)<br/><br/>Ok, the edition I read has 31 stories. Doubleday/ Nightfall, 1982. Stories originally from 1939 to 1977. Perhaps all editions the same, I dunno, but there you are. <br/><br/>It also has a nice concise introduction about Robot-as-Menace and Robot-as-Pathos and related thoughts, and is organized by theme or (slice of) world-bui</span>
  <span id="freeText12571598620501385676" style="display:none">(I, Robot, is the first collection of short stories. Second is The Rest of the Robots. Robot Dreams only has one new story in it. The Complete Robot is reported to be truly complete.)<br /><br />Ok, the edition I read has 31 stories. Doubleday/ Nightfall, 1982. Stories originally from 1939 to 1977. Perhaps all editions the same, I dunno, but there you are. <br /><br />It also has a nice concise introduction about Robot-as-Menace and Robot-as-Pathos and related thoughts, and is organized by theme or (slice of) world-built, with intros to each section, and even a Last Word, all by the author. Wonderful presentation of stories that I still enjoy after all these years, after reading them when young, finding some anthologized elsewhere, rereading, etc. <br /><br />Still thought-provoking, and entertaining, and sometimes downright moving. Asimov had the smarts to close with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25611395.The_Bicentennial_Man" title="The Bicentennial Man by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bicentennial Man</a>, a brilliant tear-jerker that moved me, and impressed me, even more this time than the others that I read it. If you're an SF fan and have not read that, you must. (It's not long, just is usually found in collections).<br /><br />This read, though, I think my favorite is Feminine Intuition. I really enjoyed being able to read all the Susan Calvin stories and that one is a good 'snap' to let the dear lady finally retire.<br /><br />If your spec. fic. book club ever wants to read a collection of short stories, you-all should choose this. Lots to discuss. Not just tech, but character motivations, meaning-of-life, future of men's fashion, etc....<br /><br />I could easily stand to read this yet again in a decade or so. ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="12571598620501385676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6589049422750499883">This includes <i>I, Robot</i> as well as a bunch of other robot stories. All in all it's an enjoyable collection. <br/><br/>Does it add much to the experience of reading <i>I, Robot</i>? Somewhat. The other stories are much the same thing in many cases and quite different in others. It's a bit jumpier in flow since it's a heavy collection, but there are some gems included here that really stood out: "The Tercentenary Incident", "Victory Unintentional", and "The Bicentennial Man". Aside from that last story, it doesn't </span>
  <span id="freeText6589049422750499883" style="display:none">This includes <i>I, Robot</i> as well as a bunch of other robot stories. All in all it's an enjoyable collection. <br /><br />Does it add much to the experience of reading <i>I, Robot</i>? Somewhat. The other stories are much the same thing in many cases and quite different in others. It's a bit jumpier in flow since it's a heavy collection, but there are some gems included here that really stood out: "The Tercentenary Incident", "Victory Unintentional", and "The Bicentennial Man". Aside from that last story, it doesn't add a whole lot to the robot experience, but it does contain some fun stuff. Also included is "Mirror Image," a story about R. Daneel Olivaw and Elijah Baley, of the Robot novels series.<br /><br />While I did enjoy reading this, I gave it one less star than <i>I, Robot</i> for two reasons. It no longer had the "Mind and Iron" binding narrative that made <i>I, Robot</i> flow smoothly from story to story. Also, by the end of the book I was honestly tired of robots.</span>

<div id="review_3306154640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3306154640" />
    <a title="Laura-Kristiina Valdson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson"><img alt="Laura-Kristiina Valdson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595963011p2/46052387.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3306154640?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura-Kristiina Valdson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura-Kristiina Valdson" href="/user/show/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson">Laura-Kristiina Valdson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson?shelf=isaac-asimov">isaac-asimov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46052387-laura-kristiina-valdson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3306154640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10676753926377832541">’’The complete Robot’’ consists of 30 short stories, written from 1939 to 1977. There’s also my personal favourite, ’’The Bicentennial Man’’. I read the novelette as a young girl and fell in love with science fiction ever since. I couldn’t stop crying after finishing it. It’s about a creative robot named Andrew, who wishes to be declared human being above anything in the world. After everything he has contributed and numerous adjustments later, he might get that wish. But only if he lets himself</span>
  <span id="freeText10676753926377832541" style="display:none">’’The complete Robot’’ consists of 30 short stories, written from 1939 to 1977. There’s also my personal favourite, ’’The Bicentennial Man’’. I read the novelette as a young girl and fell in love with science fiction ever since. I couldn’t stop crying after finishing it. It’s about a creative robot named Andrew, who wishes to be declared human being above anything in the world. After everything he has contributed and numerous adjustments later, he might get that wish. But only if he lets himself die, as human beings are mortal. <br /><br />As he says:<br />’’My own positronic pathways have lasted nearly two centuries without perceptible change and can last for centuries more. Isn’t that the fundamental barrier? Human beings can tolerate an immortal robot, for it doesn’t matter how long a machine lasts. They cannot tolerate an immortal human being, since their own mortality is endurable only so long as it is universal. And for that reason they won’t make me human being.’’<br /><br />Another one:<br />’’After all your years,’’ said Li-Hsing sadly, ’’you are still trying to reason out the human being. Poor Andrew, don’t be angry, but it’s the robot in you that drives you in that direction.’’<br /><br />I love how Asimov writes robots. They’re decent and idealistic, just like his best characters. Sometimes even more decent than the human characters. His stories usually have a twist or surprising ending that surprises the reader. He writes about human-robot relationships, class conflict, ’’the frankenstein complex’’, economy, sociology, psychology etc. As such, his stories have a broad scope. While he loves to play around with the 3 laws of robotics, Asimov certainly has a bigger message to tell with his stories. <br /><br />My favourite stories were: ’’The Bicentennial Man’’, ’’Robbie’’, ’’Someday’’, ’’Segregationist’’, ’’Victory Unintentional’’, ’’Mirror Image’’, ’’Reason’’, ’’Liar!’’ and ’’Feminine Intuition’’.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10676753926377832541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1697834621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697834621" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903197-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311861358p2/5903197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697834621?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/5903197-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=short-stories-novellas">short-stories-novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697834621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6856503508496395267">My first Asimov book and I loved it, from the first till the last story included. His <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8683655.Foundation_Trilogy' title='Foundation Trilogy by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Foundation Trilogy</a> is still waiting to be read, but as I saw this collection of short stories, I decided to tackle these first.<br/><br/>'The Complete Robot' is said to contain all of his robot stories that were published previously in other compilations or magazines, and a few other ones that didn't make it into those earlier compilations. Everything is neatly explained in the foreword (and the different introductions t</span>
  <span id="freeText6856503508496395267" style="display:none">My first Asimov book and I loved it, from the first till the last story included. His <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8683655.Foundation_Trilogy" title="Foundation Trilogy by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation Trilogy</a> is still waiting to be read, but as I saw this collection of short stories, I decided to tackle these first.<br /><br />'The Complete Robot' is said to contain all of his robot stories that were published previously in other compilations or magazines, and a few other ones that didn't make it into those earlier compilations. Everything is neatly explained in the foreword (and the different introductions to each segment in this compilation) by Mr Asimov himself, topped with a pinch of humour, which I didn't know he had. <br /><br />The various stories were put together according by theme: Non-human Robots (3), Metallic Robots (3), Immobile Robots (6), Humanoid Robots (3), Powell and Donovan (4), Susan Calvin (10) (a robot-psychologist - or someone who likes robots more than humans), Two Climaxes (2).<br /><br />Of course, the Three Laws of Robotics return throughout the book and are crucial in how robots work and interact with mankind:<br />1: A robot may not injure a human being or, through inaction, allow a human being to come to harm;<br />2: A robot must obey the orders given it by human beings except where such orders would conflict with the First Law;<br />3: A robot must protect its own existence as long as such protection does not conflict with the First or Second Law;<br /><br />About law no. 2: Which human being? A robot must therefore be able to distinguish a child from an adult, a police agent from a bank clerk, etc.<br /><br />Asimov tried to show that robots can be used for various kinds of work and tasks, some more specialized than the others. And that's how they are used today: assembly plants, computers, construction, in hospitals, self-driving cars (not fully trustworthy yet, of course), and elsewhere. We just don't always think about it or simply take it for granted. And then there's the eternal discussion about jobs: Will and do robots take away workers'/employees' jobs?<br /><br />With all those stories, Asimov offered a broad view on how robots are implemented in our lives, how they can be implemented and how they can become even human-like. And there are human-like robots today, as demonstrated by a.o. Honda, or in hospitals or geriatric places, to help the elderly. Who doesn't remember the cartoon series '<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Jetsons" rel="nofollow noopener">The Jetsons</a>' and specifically Rosie, the household robot? She's also in this book, albeit in a different version. So is an alternative version of KITT, the car in '<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knight_Rider_(1982_TV_series)" rel="nofollow noopener">Knight Rider</a>', in this case Sally.<br /><br />A few stories, one of them being 'The Tercentenary Incident', reminded me of current happenings: A president who has a robot double (why?), for example. But the robot gets destroyed during the public event, after which the real president shows up quickly to reassure the public that he's fine. Reminded me, in a way, of the coup in Turkey, the army wanting to overthrow president Erdogan.<br /><br />In another story, 'The Bicentennial Man', Andrew the robot wants to be free, but is still subjected to the Three Laws, which allows for humans to abuse this and get him to do things which are harmful to himself, despite Andrew wanting to become a human being and going at great lengths to obtain his goal, even it means a quick death. But it also shows how humanity will always have a sly way to abuse others, robots or otherwise. And how people aren't ready yet to fully accept robots as equals, unless perhaps in a certain animal shape.<br /><br />Or, if you want to go extreme: What if - but that's a what if many of us won't experience anymore, I think - robots become so free in thinking and communicating that they stand up against their makers?<br /><br />Although there's a bit of hard SF, Asimov's writing style is quite accessible here. If you haven't read any Asimov yet (or none of his robot stories), this is a fine book to start with, since it contains all of the robot stories, more than in the previous compilations. This is also a fine work for those interested in the possible happenings in the future of robotics or how every day life could look many years from now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6856503508496395267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6000924754213628739" style="display:none">Daughter loved the Robot stories from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41804.I__Robot__Robot___0_1_" title="I, Robot (Robot, #0.1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">I, Robot</a> and wanted more. We plan to track those down soon. To quote my daughter, "Isaac Asimov is a great writer!"</span>

  <span id="freeText6905773107575926706" style="display:none">All stories grip you, and some of the stories are absolutely brilliant and leave a large amount of after thought.<br /><br />Of the ones I enjoyed most are -<br /><br />1. <span id="freeTextContainer13638875621557988544"><u>
  <b>Some Nonhuman Robots</b>

  <b>Some Immobile Robots</b>

  <b>Some Metallic Robots</b>
</u><br/><br/>Victory Unintentional - 3.5<br/>Stranger In Paradise - 2.5<br/>Light Verse - 3.5<br/>Segregationist - 5<br/>Robbie - 3 *<br/><br/><u>
  <b>Some Humanoid Robots</b>

  <b>Powell and Donovan</b>
</u><br/><br/>First Law - 2<br/>Runaround - 2.5 *<br/>Reason - 4 *<br/>Catch That Rabbit! - 3 *<br/><br/><br/><u>
  <b>Susan Calvin</b>
</u><br/><br/>Liar! -  4 *<br/>Satisfaction Guaranteed - 4<br/>Len</span>
  <span id="freeText13638875621557988544" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Some Nonhuman Robots</b>
</u><br /><br />A Boys best friend - 3.5<br />Sally - 2.5 <br />Someday - 3.5<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Some Immobile Robots</b>
</u><br /><br />Point of view - 2.5<br />Think! - 3<br />True Love - 4<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Some Metallic Robots</b>
</u><br /><br />Victory Unintentional - 3.5<br />Stranger In Paradise - 2.5<br />Light Verse - 3.5<br />Segregationist - 5<br />Robbie - 3 *<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Some Humanoid Robots</b>
</u><br /><br />Let's Get Together - 3<br />Mirror Image - 3<br />The Tercentenary Incident - 4<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Powell and Donovan</b>
</u><br /><br />First Law - 2<br />Runaround - 2.5 *<br />Reason - 4 *<br />Catch That Rabbit! - 3 *<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Susan Calvin</b>
</u><br /><br />Liar! -  4 *<br />Satisfaction Guaranteed - 4<br />Lenny - 4.5<br />Galley Slave - 4.5<br />Little Lost Robot - 3.5 *<br />Risk - 3<br />Escape! - 2.5 *<br />Evidence - 4 *<br />The Evitable Conflict - 2 *<br />The Female Intuition - 3.5<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Two Climaxes</b>
</u><br /><br />Thou Art Mindful Of Him - 4<br />The Bicentennial Man - 3.5<br /><br />* Collected in I Robot <br /><br />This has been sat on my shelf for a while. There's something about an author you're not fond of and a 700 page book that's just not that inviting...<br />However, I Robot was announced as a group read and, seeing as The Complete Robot contained all of the same stories (minus the Dr. Calvin interviews), I figured what better time to pick it up? <br /><br />I found it a real slog to start with. There's no refuting Asimov's ideas and what he brought to the genre, but I have often found him to be a pretty poor storyteller, particularly when it comes to endings; and this struck mostly true for the first half of the collection, making it a real trial to wade through. There were exceptions of course, as can be gathered from my rating of each story (above), and my enjoyment definitely reached a high when I came to the Susan Calvin stories. Not just because I found her a great character, but because it was at that point that the book became much more than just a collection of short stories. There was a bigger picture, an overarching story detailing the evolution of robotics and it's gradual acceptance by humanity. The stories were pretty much chronological with recurring characters and this made it a greater joy to read the good stories, and less of a chore in reading the weaker ones. <br />In fact, despite its inconsistency, I feel that reading this collection has birthed in me a stronger desire to read Asimov (but not too much). I'll certainly be proceeding with the "Robot" series.... When I get around to it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13638875621557988544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698078051" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698078051?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Baird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Baird" href="/user/show/18839391-david-baird">David Baird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698078051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer222002284479889801">I read a lot of Asimov's robot short stories in my early teens, but never the novels and neither the Foundation books. Having discovered that the robot books are a prelude to Foundation I was intrigued to revisit.<br/><br/>I have to say that as stories they're a mixed bag. The early ones are not very well written,but do introduce important concepts into the robots' evolutions - rather fable like in many ways. I found the prose forced and the characters shallow, added to that the early robots were treated </span>
  <span id="freeText222002284479889801" style="display:none">I read a lot of Asimov's robot short stories in my early teens, but never the novels and neither the Foundation books. Having discovered that the robot books are a prelude to Foundation I was intrigued to revisit.<br /><br />I have to say that as stories they're a mixed bag. The early ones are not very well written,but do introduce important concepts into the robots' evolutions - rather fable like in many ways. I found the prose forced and the characters shallow, added to that the early robots were treated in an apartheid manner - I'm not sure if this was intentional, or rather a sign if the times when they were written, but they make uncomfortable reading at times.<br /><br />Over time though, Asimov's writing skill improved and he had rounder characters to work with and by using them over several stories they began to take on lives of their own - Susan Calvin being the most notable, if not the most lovable.<br /><br />In many ways, the whole book is setting the scene for the final story, The Bicentennial Man. This masterwork of the sci-fi genre surely stirs the emotion of tone that has read it, but takes on further poignancy in this context. It ties up the collection nicely drawing together the philosophical discussion from the preceding tales.<br /><br />Now onto The Caves of Steel!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="222002284479889801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156596406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156596406" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156596406?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156596406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13275070248865538625"><i>Almost</i> one-stop shopping for all your robots-by-Asimov needs. Most, but not all, of Asimov's robot and robot-like stories are included here, including all of the stories from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41804.I__Robot__Robot___0_1_' title='I, Robot (Robot, #0.1) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>I, Robot</a>. I wouldn't suggest reading this instead, of course, because you're missing all of the wonderful bridging narration. Even having already read I, Robot, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41818.Robot_Dreams__Robot___0_4_' title='Robot Dreams (Robot, #0.4) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robot Dreams</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41823.Robot_Visions__Robot___0_5_' title='Robot Visions (Robot, #0.5) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robot Visions</a>, I still found plenty of stories that were new to me. Exciting, for me, and it made reading the book more than worthwhile. I loved i</span>
  <span id="freeText13275070248865538625" style="display:none"><i>Almost</i> one-stop shopping for all your robots-by-Asimov needs. Most, but not all, of Asimov's robot and robot-like stories are included here, including all of the stories from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41804.I__Robot__Robot___0_1_" title="I, Robot (Robot, #0.1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">I, Robot</a>. I wouldn't suggest reading this instead, of course, because you're missing all of the wonderful bridging narration. Even having already read I, Robot, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41818.Robot_Dreams__Robot___0_4_" title="Robot Dreams (Robot, #0.4) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Robot Dreams</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41823.Robot_Visions__Robot___0_5_" title="Robot Visions (Robot, #0.5) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Robot Visions</a>, I still found plenty of stories that were new to me. Exciting, for me, and it made reading the book more than worthwhile. I loved it, but I would really only recommend it to readers who are completely addicted to Asimov's robots, enough so that they want to read everything. It's too big of a chunk to be an entry into that world. But if you have read and loved the robot books, this is a natural next step.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17779596717769780544">This is a collection of Asimov's robot based short stories. I have previously read I Robot and all of those stories are also here/ This collection, however, also includes many other stories that were not found there and so they were new to me.   <span id="freeText17779596717769780544" style="display:none">This is a collection of Asimov's robot based short stories. I have previously read I Robot and all of those stories are also here/ This collection, however, also includes many other stories that were not found there and so they were new to me. What seemed unique to me was that, besides a couple stories very early on, each story here is placed in a sort of loose chronology. As you move further into the book you are also moving further forward in fictional time. In this way the book, while still maintaining the anthology feel, also seems to be something more. It is more as though you are getting a snapshot from different points on a (future) historical timeline. <br /><br />If you like classic sci-fi you will probably really like this book. If you don't... then why are you even reading this review? </span>
